<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 18pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino; color: #ffffff; background-color: #808080;"><b><span style="line-height: 115%;">Spiritual Message for the Day – Gurudev’s Satsanga by Sri Swami Venkatesananda</span></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;">&nbsp;<strong style="text-indent: -0.5in;"><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Baba Times Digest© | 11 September 2015 15.04 EST | New York Edition</span></span></span></strong></p>
<hr />
<div>
<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" hspace="0" vspace="0" align="left">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td valign="top" align="left" style="padding-top: 0in; padding-right: 9.0pt; padding-bottom: 0in; padding-left: 9.0pt;">
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Gurudev’s Satsanga<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Divine Life Society Publication: </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/download/integral.htm#_VPID_25"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Sivananda’s Integral Yoga</b></span></a></span><b> by </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/saints/venkates.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Sri Swami Venkatesananda</b></span></a></span><b><o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Gurudev’s satsanga was itself unique in many ways. It was very beautiful and wonderful, and combined songs in praise of the Lord, chanting his names, music, study of scriptures, discourses etc. It catered and appealed to the needs and temperaments of all; it satisfied everyone’s hunger. In the early days, there were only about ten or fifteen of us and perhaps ten visitors. We all sat in two rows and there was a little altar with a wick lamp on it. There was also a hurricane lantern on a small stool, which had to be passed around to help some of us read from the scriptures. The satsanga started with: </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">om om om </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> jaya ganesha jaya ganesha jaya ganesha pahimam </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> sri ganesha sri ganesha sri ganesha raksha mam </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> jaya guru siva guru hari guru ram </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> jagadguru paramguru sadguru shyam </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> adi guru advaita guru ananda guru om </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> chidguru chidghana guru chinmaya guru om </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> hare rama hare rama rama rama hare hare </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> hare krishna hare krishna krishna krishna hare hare </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> (later this was greatly expanded)</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Then the lamp was passed to the first person sitting on the Master’s left, who would read a chapter of the Gita, with or without translation. As soon as that was finished, that person would lead in chanting a kirtan and then the lantern would be pushed to the next person, who read from some other scripture. This person would also lead the next kirtan. And so it would go round. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Sometimes the Master used to ask somebody or other to read an article which he had written that day. This was very interesting. Someone might have gone to him to complain that someone else rebuked him in anger. The Master did not rebuke the person who rebuked because it might hurt him. Instead he would write a nice article, “The danger of anger”. (Sometimes he would give it to the person concerned to type.) He would bring it to the satsanga to be read by the one who lost his temper. It hits home! It is meant for him. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">From there on, everyone had to lead in singing a kirtan. It was not enough to sing in chorus. The Master would not accept any excuse or explanation. He pointed out that shyness was an obstacle to spiritual progress. When everyone had finished, the Master would conclude with the mahamantra kirtan and the mahamrityunjaya mantra. The satsang concluded with arati and the most sublime peace chants, beautifully expressive of his innermost feelings; </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Om sarvesam svastir bhavatu, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> sarvesam santir bhavatu, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> sarvesam purnam bhavatu, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> sarvesam mangalam bhavatu, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> sarve bhavantu sukhinah, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> sarve santu niramayah, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> sarve bhadrani pasyantu, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> ma kaschit duhkha-bhagbhavet. </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> asato ma sat gamaya, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> tamaso ma jyotir gamaya, </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> mrityor ma amritam gamaya. </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> Om purnamadah purnamidam </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> purnat purnamudachyate </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> purnasya purnamadaya </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> purnameva vasistyate </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> Om santih santih santih</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The spirit of the above chants is as follows: “May all be blessed with well-being, auspiciousness, peace and fullness. May all be happy and free from illness. May all see only good; and may no ill befall anyone. O Lord, lead me from the unreal to the real, from darkness to light and from mortality to immortality. The Lord is full; the creation is also full. The latter has appeared in the Lord, and yet the Lord is everfull. Om. Peace. Peace. Peace.” </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">After this the Master would walk away very quietly so that the profound thoughts and ideas heard from the scriptures would still be fresh and ringing in our minds and heart as we went to bed. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">This was the whole basic structure of the satsanga. Gurudev encouraged people to have satsanga in their own homes, perhaps with a few neighbours, choosing their own scriptures. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">om tryambakam yajamahe sugandhim pustivardhanam </span><br /><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> urvarukamiva bandhanan mrtyor muksiya mamrtat.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">(We worship the Lord who promotes health and strength. May he liberate us from death).</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;">&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><span class="MsoHyperlink"><b>Excerpts from: </b></span><b>Gurudev’s Satsanga - </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/download/integral.htm#_VPID_25"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Sivananda’s Integral Yoga</b></span></a></span><b> by </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/saints/venkates.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Sri Swami Venkatesananda</b></span></a></span></span><b><span style="font-size: 9.0pt;"><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</div>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span style="font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino; font-size: 12pt;">&nbsp;</span></p>
